  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b4108a44-8435-4a04-8876-7fca057b1264'
      });
    }

She seeks refuge at a rehab for wayward immortals, where she meets the gorgeous, undeniably sexy Reyn, who seems inexplicably linked to her past.<br /><br />Nastasya finally begins to deal with life, and even feels safe--until the night she learns that someone wants her dead.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes and No. <br/>No there aren't any characters referred to as witches, BUT all the main cast uses magic heavily influenced by real life witchcraft (such a<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes and No. <br />No there aren't any characters referred to as witches, BUT all the main cast uses magic heavily influenced by real life witchcraft (such as use of futhark runes, candles, crystals, herbs ect) and it is one of the main overarching themes of the book series.<br /><br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer351745111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16906317914389340456"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2014/08/review-immortal-beloved-by-cate-tiernan.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>Have you ever discovered a new book, by a new author, and absolutely LOVED it, so you go out and immediately buy the next book the author writes, and it's not <em>quite</em> as good as the first one, but it's still pretty good, so the next time a new book is released by that same author, <em>again</em>, you go out and buy it immediately, only <em>this</em> time it's not very good at all, and you start to think maybe the author is a one hit wonder?<------that's a REALLY long, yet (mostly?) grammatic</span>
  <span id="freeText16906317914389340456" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/08/review-immortal-beloved-by-cate-tiernan.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br /><br />Have you ever discovered a new book, by a new author, and absolutely LOVED it, so you go out and immediately buy the next book the author writes, and it's not <em>quite</em> as good as the first one, but it's still pretty good, so the next time a new book is released by that same author, <em>again</em>, you go out and buy it immediately, only <em>this</em> time it's not very good at all, and you start to think maybe the author is a one hit wonder?&lt;------that's a REALLY long, yet (mostly?) grammatically correct, sentence.<br /><br />That's also really NOT what happened here. In fact, it was pretty much the reverse.<br /><br />I discovered Tiernan's SWEEP series probably 10 years and inhaled it (all 15 installments). It was <em>okay</em>, but the most I can say about it is that it was entertaining. Then I found her BALEFIRE series, which was thankfully much shorter (only 4 installments) and it blew SWEEP out the water.<br /><br />So when I stumbled across IMMORTAL BELOVED, I was like, "Ooohhh . . . that looks interesting."<br /><br />And it was fantastic.<br /><br />Nastasya, Nasty to her friends, is an immortal. No one is sure where the first immortal came from, but they can be found among every race and nationality. As is usually the case, they are not <em>truly</em> immortal--if you cut off their heads, burn their bodies, and scatter their ashes, they will not survive, but that's a rather specific set of circumstances, so I don't begrudge them their "immortal" status.<br /><br />They also have the ability to learn and use magic.<br /><br />If you know anything about Tiernan, then this is not a surprise. Tiernan excels at writing all things witchy, and IMMORTAL BELOVED is no exception. But Nasty avoids her magic, b/c she learned at a very young age how dangerous it was for her to let others learn of her abilities.<br /><br />Why is it dangerous . . . ? I think you know where I'm going with this--READ THE BOOK *winks*<br /><br />But Nastasya can no longer avoid her magic when she leaves the life she's been living in London, and the friends she's been living it with for the last hundred years, behind.<br /><br />This book . . . is a very emotional story to read. Nasty has money and beauty and immortality and a collection of friends who have all of those things as well, and . . . they're pretty damn awful to tell the truth. Nasty leaves without a word after Incy, her best friend, uses magic to break the back of a rude cabbie . . . b/c he can. B/c he was angry that the cabbie dared to call them out for their juvenile behavior. So he . . . broke the poor man's back . . . left him in a puddle on the street beside his cab . . . used magic again to prevent the man from calling out for help . . . and then went clubbing.<br /><br />YEP. Incy's kind of a bastard.<br /><br />And while Nasty is shocked and horrified by Incy's behavior--she had no idea he could use magic that way--she allows herself to be steered towards the bar that the rest of her crew are headed for, starts drinking, and does not one thing to help the man.<br /><br />The next day, she wakes up hungover and completely disgusted with herself, and decides that something has to change. She has no idea how she became the person she currently is, but she's terrified of what it might mean for the rest of her very long life.<br /><br />So she runs to the states.<br /><br />She'd met a women about 80 years ago, you see, who told her simply to come if she decided she wanted more out of life.<br /><br />So she does.<br /><br />From there she enters a kind of rehab for immortals. It's hard and it <em>hurts</em>, but Nastasya has reached a place where no matter how bad it is with River and the other immortals at the retreat, she can't stand the thought of being anywhere else either . . . so she stays.<br /><br />This book would be an excellent story even without the paranormal elements. Nasty doesn't need to be an immortal or capable of magic for her story to draw you in, make you feel her agony and despair and determination to change, be better, be MORE. But she is . . . and that only makes things more interesting . . .<br /><br />And then there's Reyn . . . the Viking GOD. Well, okay fine, he's not <em>really</em> a god, but he's several inches over six feet of blond Viking warrior, and that's good enough for me.<br /><br />And they HATE each other. It's fantastic. Nastasya and Reyn achieve the kind of slow burn combustibility that's only possible when legitimate dislike is present, and it's HOT.<br /><br />So the characters are awesome. And despite what I said earlier about no one really knowing where immortals came from, the world-building in this series is VERY cool. It's a mix of mythology and paganism, and I loved it. AND b/c even the youngest characters are as old or older than your grandparents, and no part of this story takes place on a high school campus, this is one of those YA novels that even readers 10+ years out of high school can enjoy. IMMORTAL BELOVED is an excellent first installment to this excellent trilogy. I recommend it to anyone who likes witchy UF and hot Viking <s>gods</s>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16906317914389340456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_92739688" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92739688" />
    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92739688?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316035910" href="/book/show/8961636-immortal-beloved">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to oliviasbooks by: </span>
      Melanie
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=favorites-of-2011">favorites-of-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=hug-them-lick-them-favorites">hug-them-lick-them-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=stays-with-me">stays-with-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=love-story-romance">love-story-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=i-cannot-tell-you-my-secret">i-cannot-tell-you-my-secret</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92739688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17639050493435366483"><i>2016:</i> Isn't it utterly marvelous, when a favorite aces the re-reading experience with flying colors after almost five years?<br/><br/><i>2011:</i> I can't really comprehend that I am sitting here pressing determinedly the five-star-button - in spite of the first chapters, which obviously have been patched together rather sloppily and almost caused me to switch books with one click on my Kindle, ... <i>and</i> in spite of the undeniable cliffy. Yet - here I am am doing precisely that and feeling completely comfortable w</span>
  <span id="freeText17639050493435366483" style="display:none"><i>2016:</i> Isn't it utterly marvelous, when a favorite aces the re-reading experience with flying colors after almost five years?<br /><br /><i>2011:</i> I can't really comprehend that I am sitting here pressing determinedly the five-star-button - in spite of the first chapters, which obviously have been patched together rather sloppily and almost caused me to switch books with one click on my Kindle, ... <i>and</i> in spite of the undeniable cliffy. Yet - here I am am doing precisely that and feeling completely comfortable with it.<br /><br />Really, at the beginning I had the fleeting, horrible impression my paranormal "favorite" <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7744064.Infinite_Days__Vampire_Queen___1_" title="Infinite Days (Vampire Queen, #1) by Rebecca Maizel" rel="nofollow noopener">Infinite Days</a> would manage to catch up with me. The cruel, excitement-addicted, immortal heroine - unable to feel for mere mortals - and her gang of equally shiny, but worthless companions, who break a taxi driver's spine for fun. I got very angry about repetitive sentences that should have been edited away and I moaned about unbelievable scenarios like an immortal girl hiding a burn-mark from her best friend under a scarf for over a hundred years - in spite of drunken and drugged party nights, shared hotel rooms and beach holidays, or like the same girl being shocked about said best-friend's pleasure at causing someone deadly pain. As if it would be possible to hide a personality this rotten for over a century from someone that close to you. <br /><br />I held out and was rewarded with 180-degrees-style improvement. From the moment Natasya boarded the plane in order to leave her old life behind, the nasty crinkles smoothed out and the story enfolded beautifully in front of my eyes. And Natasya/Lilja "magickally" wormed herself into a cosy nook of my heart - the one reserved for heroines, who are prickly and nasty and damaged on the outside, but hurt and helpless and lovable deep within. <br /><br />"Immortal Beloved" could probably be described as a cross between <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9301.Rachel_s_Holiday__Walsh_Family___2_" title="Rachel's Holiday (Walsh Family, #2) by Marian Keyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel's Holiday</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5083254.Secrets_of_Truth_and_Beauty" title="Secrets of Truth and Beauty by Megan Frazer Blakemore" rel="nofollow noopener">Secrets of Truth and Beauty</a> and maybe <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/235718.Succubus_Blues__Georgina_Kincaid___1_" title="Succubus Blues (Georgina Kincaid, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Succubus Blues</a>. It is the story of a girl whose long, long life has made her unable to feel attachment, unable to sleep without "self-medication", unable to decide for herself what she really wants. It is a story of a girl at the point of no return. A girl who turns herself in at a rehabilitation center for wayward immortals, because she vaguely remembers a woman inviting her 50 years ago to come and stay with her should she hit the bottom end of things and change her mind. The rehab plot unexpectedly uncovered some very interesting strings of thought about the burdens of immortality, but also about a fulfilled life in general. That might have easliy turned into something preachy-soppy, but Natasya's own snarky, sceptical attitude and her ongoing inner monologue fueled by exaggeration lightens the mood and gives her stay at "River's Edge" a pretty hilarious note. <br /><br />I was really relieved not to have to read about the hot-hot-hot love-interest without reprieve. He is of the - in my opinion - hot sort and I began to look forward to Natasya's encounters with him (nothing like enemies falling for each other hard, isn't there), but I was glad that the romance was not taking over the already interesting story as soon as the potential supernatural heartbreaker made his first entrance.<br /><br />I have to say, I not only guessed the connection between Natasya and Reyn, I really <i>knew</i> when she implied that his face looked familiar. But at that point I did not mind anymore. I was too much enamoured already to care. <br /><br />So. Same as with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9462812.Die_for_Me__Revenants___1_" title="Die for Me (Revenants, #1) by Amy Plum" rel="nofollow noopener">Die for Me</a> for instance, falling in love with this book has been an entirely individual process that cannot be easily explained by check-marking off its shining points. Thus it makes recommending it to all my friends a tricky thing. I won't do it to be on the safe side. I certainly do not want to be lynched. But realize that maybe you are missing out on something rather satisfying and heart-cuddling. <br /><br />I, for my part, crave to read the sequel now. But ... I, too, know what a sequel can do to a lovely story (exasperated sigh).</span>
  <a data-text-id="17639050493435366483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1927025628?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bgurl (don&#39;t h8 me cuz I&#39;m honestful)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bgurl (don&#39;t h8 me cuz I&#39;m honestful)" href="/user/show/4166814-bgurl-don-t-h8-me-cuz-i-m-honestful">Bgurl (don&#39;t h8 me cuz I&#39;m honestful)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4166814-bgurl-don-t-h8-me-cuz-i-m-honestful?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4166814-bgurl-don-t-h8-me-cuz-i-m-honestful?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4166814-bgurl-don-t-h8-me-cuz-i-m-honestful?shelf=war-death-and-destruction">war-death-and-destruction</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4166814-bgurl-don-t-h8-me-cuz-i-m-honestful?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4166814-bgurl-don-t-h8-me-cuz-i-m-honestful?shelf=orphans">orphans</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4166814-bgurl-don-t-h8-me-cuz-i-m-honestful?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4166814-bgurl-don-t-h8-me-cuz-i-m-honestful?shelf=heroine-snarky">heroine-snarky</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4166814-bgurl-don-t-h8-me-cuz-i-m-honestful?shelf=romance-secondary">romance-secondary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4166814-bgurl-don-t-h8-me-cuz-i-m-honestful?shelf=keeps-you-guessing">keeps-you-guessing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1927025628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8221862745953410155"><b><i>Immortal Beloved (IB 01)</i> by Cate Tiernan: 2 “Captain Obvious” Stars.</b><br/><br/><i>“I’m here because I can’t bear to be not-here anymore. I’m here because I can’t tell right from wrong, light from dark. I’m here because I can’t stand being me." ~ Nastasya</i><br/> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478931887ra/21129969.gif' width='300' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>In the 1960s, her name was Hope.</b> In the 1920s, Christiane. In the 1500s, Sunna. Before that, another name. A name she never thinks of. A name she’s running from, but can’t. And she’s tired. Tired of being cynical. Tired of being lonely. Tired of being numb. <br/> </span>
  <span id="freeText8221862745953410155" style="display:none"><b><i>Immortal Beloved (IB 01)</i> by Cate Tiernan: 2 “Captain Obvious” Stars.</b><br><br><i>“I’m here because I can’t bear to be not-here anymore. I’m here because I can’t tell right from wrong, light from dark. I’m here because I can’t stand being me." ~ Nastasya</i><br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478931887ra/21129969.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>In the 1960s, her name was Hope.</b> In the 1920s, Christiane. In the 1500s, Sunna. Before that, another name. A name she never thinks of. A name she’s running from, but can’t. And she’s tired. Tired of being cynical. Tired of being lonely. Tired of being numb. <br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478931887ra/21129970.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“ ‘Like what?’ I asked.<br>She shook her head, her brown eyes sad. ‘You can have so much more, be so much more.’ ” ~ Nastasya &amp; River</i><br><br><b> In the 16th century, she was a farmer and a servant.</b> In the 17th Century, she survived the great plague. She saw French royalty beheaded. Lost a husband in the Anglo-Indian Wars. Sipped champagne while dancing The Charleston. And turned on, tuned in, and dropped out with the Hollywood elite. By the 21st century, she’d been everywhere. Done everything. Invented the frigging T-shirt! She doesn’t know what “more” there could possibly be. But she wants to find out. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489093843ra/22185387.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“ ‘I want to be myself. I want my power back. I want to be my mother’s daughter, my father’s heir.’ My voice choked up.<br>A new light flared in River’s eyes. ‘Yes. I want that for you.’ ” <br>~ Nastasya &amp; River</i><br><br><b>For 450 years, she’s been running, now it’s time to stop.</b> It’s time to confront her past. Face her fears. Discover what she is. Who she is. And who she’s destined to become. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478931887ra/21129972.gif" width="375" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“Being good is something we choose every day, throughout the day, for the rest of our life. A day is made of a thousand decisions, most small, some huge. With each decision, you can work toward light or sink toward darkness. The point of life isn’t to be good all the time. It’s to be as good as you can. No one’s perfect. No one does it right all the time. That’s not what life is." ~ Asher</i><br><br><b>Some writers subtly weave life lessons into their text so it feels organic to the story. </b> Tales such as these are often an adventure, as messages aren’t easily identifiable, and different readers interpret the same story in different ways. Cate Tiernan is not a subtle writer. Hence, the life lessons imparted in <i>Immortal Beloved</i> are blatantly obvious. So be forewarned: if you’re not a fan of “In Your Face” moralizing, you may want to avoid this series.<br><br>For a more detailed critique of this book, check out Mara's review: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296949438?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Click Me Baby!</a><br><br><b>Links to my reviews of books 2 &amp; 3:</b><br><i>Darkness Falls (IB #2):</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1937315378?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Click Me Again!</a><br><i>Eternally Yours (IB #3):</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1948914200?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Click Again (you know you want to!)</a><br><br><i>For information about my rating system, see my profile page.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8221862745953410155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_267447434" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/267447434" />
    <a title="Sophia." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6520961-sophia"><img alt="Sophia." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322479535p2/6520961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/267447434?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia." href="/user/show/6520961-sophia">Sophia.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=cliche-love-story">cliche-love-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=so-very-weak">so-very-weak</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=eye-rolls-and-frowning">eye-rolls-and-frowning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=too-cliche">too-cliche</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=popular-girl-gone-freaky">popular-girl-gone-freaky</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=too-superficial">too-superficial</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=stupid-hero">stupid-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=unbelievable">unbelievable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=unsatisfaying-ending">unsatisfaying-ending</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267447434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18103396180399790636">So I took a Mary Sue test for this book and it included questions such as:<br/><blockquote>14. Does your character have a scar or other small "flaw" that is noticed by someone, but does not actually detract from your character's appearance from your point of view? <b>Check.</b><br/><br/>42. Does your character always have money to spend on frivolities or whatever she really wants or needs at the time? <br/>For no apparent reason? (<u>EG, your character never works or gives any clue to any source of income.</u>) <b>Check.</b><br/><br/>52. Your character alon</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText18103396180399790636" style="display:none">So I took a Mary Sue test for this book and it included questions such as:<br /><blockquote>14. Does your character have a scar or other small "flaw" that is noticed by someone, but does not actually detract from your character's appearance from your point of view? <b>Check.</b><br /><br />42. Does your character always have money to spend on frivolities or whatever she really wants or needs at the time? <br />For no apparent reason? (<u>EG, your character never works or gives any clue to any source of income.</u>) <b>Check.</b><br /><br />52. Your character alone uses a weapon that: <br /><blockquote>a.Is famous or legendary before the character acquires it? <br />b.Was given by some kind of spirit/magical being? <br />c.Is magical? <b>Check.</b><br /></blockquote> <br />75. Is your character some kind of 'chosen one' and/or a major part of a prophecy? <b>Check.</b><br /><br />78. On the subject of your character and her family... <br /><blockquote>a.Was your character orphaned, abandoned, kicked out, or at least raised by a family/person that was not her own family? <b>Check.</b><br />b.Was a major villain responsible for the death of the parents or guardians? <b>Check.</b><br />c.Was your character responsible for the death of her parents/guardians?<br />d.Did your character witnessed the death of the parents/guardians? <b>Check.</b><br />e.Was she adopted by a cruel family or person? <br />f.Ran away at any point? <b>Check.</b><br />g.Raised herself? <b>Check.</b><br />h.Lived in the streets? <b>Check.</b><br />i.The very last or only survivor of anything? <b>Check.</b><br />j.Adopted by another species/racial group?</blockquote><blockquote></blockquote><br />And there are so many more questions. I'll just skip them and go straight to the result: <br /><blockquote>36+ : Fanfiction authors, you might just want to start over. Role-players and original fiction authors, at this point your characters are likely to provoke eye-rolling and exclaimations of "yeah, right!" from your readers. (Well, at least from me.) Immediate workover is probably in order. </blockquote><br />Haha! <i>Awesome</i>. I wonder if Cate Tierman knows about that test.<br /><br />I hated the writing. First there are the random "OMG", "WTF", "ha ha ha", "whatever", "you know", and the infamous "I mean, I'm telling it like it is, people!" (yeah, that's directed to you, reader). Second, the book is weirdly written and suspiciously drafty. There's a sentence at the beginning she says : "Maybe it was in the 70's. Or was it in the sixties?" Well, which one is it? 1970's and 1960's or seventies and sixties? <br /><br />Characterization: Reyn is a joke, he's some kind of washed-out copy of Dimitri Belikov's twin brother. Only with even less personality (and believe me, I did not think this was possible). Are we supposed to swoon? The descriptions throughout the book are terrible.<br /><br />And I kept thinking that there was going to be a twist at the end because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[really, Nell is the culprit? Come the fuck on. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, I think the major problem for me is that I am a huge Anne Rice fan. When it comes to vampires in literature, if you've read and liked Anne Rice, how could this book ever compare? <br /><br />If you want to read about immortals who've been walking the earth for centuries in excruciating anguish; who drown in despair because they can't tell whether they're damned or just undead; creatures who shed tears of blood because they are unable to feel their own heartbeats... Read Anne Rice. Her vampires saga is pure magic. Granted - she also has her flaws, but it's still so much more valuable than this book. And immortality is a subject that has way too much potential to be treated as casually as it is dealt with here.<br /><br />In this book, Nastasya kept dropping random informations like "I was in France during the Revolution" or "I was sick with TB in Taïwan in 1618"... But none of it feels real, you know? You don't believe it for a second. She just drops countries and time periods because that's what she's supposed to do, being 456 years old. But it's just so shallow, you never really enter the world that Tiernan tried to create.<br /><br />I thought of the best way to finish this review, and honestly, I'll just leave you with a quote from Interview of the Vampire. This is when vampire Lestat turns soft-hearted Louis into a vampire against his will - condemning him to an immortal life which may only perdure by murdering a victim each night - and he tries to explain that Louis now has to let go of all human remorse, for he has just entered a fabulous new world: <br /><blockquote>“Evil is a point of view. We are immortal. And what we have before us are the rich feasts that conscience cannot appreciate and mortal men cannot know without regret. God kills, and so shall we; indiscriminately He takes the richest and the poorest, and so shall we; for no creatures under God are as we are, none so like Him as ourselves, dark angels not confined to the stinking limits of hell but wandering His earth and all its kingdoms.”</blockquote><br />... And now a quote from Immortal Beloved: <br /><blockquote>“Now he was kissing me, not in a scary way, not with hostility, but with warm, seductive intent. In a hayloft, in the barn, in the middle of the night. This scene brought to you by the letters W, T, and F.”</blockquote><br />I rest my case.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="18103396180399790636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_471576547" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/471576547" />
    <a title="Kristalia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia"><img alt="Kristalia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535637983p2/5705623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/471576547?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristalia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristalia " href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia">Kristalia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316035910" href="/book/show/8961636-immortal-beloved">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=unique-or-different-story">unique-or-different-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=made-me-smile-or-laugh">made-me-smile-or-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=cut-my-heart-out">cut-my-heart-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-couple">favorite-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=be-my-heroes-please">be-my-heroes-please</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=me-likey-mucho">me-likey-mucho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=be-my-heroine-please">be-my-heroine-please</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer471576547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10023558028298795431"><b>Final rating: 4.75/5 stars</b><br/><b>Final rating - for the whole series: 4.75/5 stars</b><br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399972i/774567.jpg' width='400' height='225' alt='review img' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was so cool. I like it that this book is about immortal meeting immortal, and as it seems, falling in love with immortal, and making awkward situations with immortal, instead of immortal falling in love with human. I have seen that story way too many times. This is something new. And i like it :D I was getting tired of the overused paranormal-human. And there is actually very little of romance between the characters</span>
  <span id="freeText10023558028298795431" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 4.75/5 stars</b><br><b>Final rating - for the whole series: 4.75/5 stars</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399972i/774567.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="review img" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was so cool. I like it that this book is about immortal meeting immortal, and as it seems, falling in love with immortal, and making awkward situations with immortal, instead of immortal falling in love with human. I have seen that story way too many times. This is something new. And i like it :D I was getting tired of the overused paranormal-human. And there is actually very little of romance between the characters, which i also liked. Oh and it is also <i> mature ya </i>, which is awesome &lt;3 And i loved the writing, because i dont like this style where there is only one POV, and from female's perspective, but this was nice and very good :D<br><blockquote>“Being good is something that one must choose over and over again, every day, throughout the day, for the rest of one’s life,” Asher said. “A day is made of a thousand decisions, most small, some huge. With each decision, you have the chance to work toward light or sink toward darkness.”</blockquote><br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Story</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br>The story itself was interesting as well. Its about immortals, their lives, and powers. Magick powers xD....(why not magic).....Anyway, as it seems, all immortals are born as Dark - Terävä, and they can gradually become Light again - Tähti . MC called Nastasya, Dark immortal, is trying to escape her group when their evil passed the limits she could bear. And escaping, she found that she had done some things that she wasn't exactly proud of. She then remembers an immortal called River who said that Nasty is welcome to come to her place. <br><br>In River's Edge, she learns how to appreciate life, nature, everything around her; that by caring about herself, she will care about the others as well. Nasty then tries to live her life in whole different way that she was used to. But going Light doesn't mean staying Light forever, there will always be situations where she/they could revert to Dark in matter of seconds. <br><br> <blockquote>“None of us here just decided one day to embrace good, or light, and leave darkness behind forever,” Asher said patiently. “It’s not a decision you make once. Being Terävä is how we’re born, but not how we have to stay. Being Tähti can be achieved, but once it’s achieved, it’s easily lost again.” </blockquote><br><br>But story itself is kinda slow, without action, so there is no fights between the immortals or using their powers. This is more of the type with how immortals choose to live their looooong lives, although there is always way to die-beheading. Also, the part that was in the synopsis about someone trying to kill her, happens around 70% of the book...So yeah.......xD<br><br>But, the story hides something interesting, and that was interesting. Some parts of it will probably be important in the next books though.<br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Characters</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br>This is also one of the rare books where i actually support the heroine way to much, and i am basically in love with her. Nastasya is ideal type of heroines i love and those are rare. <br><br>There are also a lot of characters, 13 in River's edge: the 4 teachers-River, Solis, Asher (who was River’s partner), and Anne, and students: Daisuke, Reyn, Nell, Rachel, Charles, Brynne, Lorenz &amp; Jess. And in her previous group: Stratton, Innocencio, Cicely, Boz &amp; Katy.... Like i said, many characters :D And the others: Old MacIntyre, his daughter Meriwether, Dray(short for Andrea)- aka goth girl.... and soooooooooo on xD<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Nastasya </u>
  </i>
</b>: She is very interesting type, and i could just connect with her. She is in other words, awesome. She had some awkward situations and i found her cute as well. She is not self centered or too confident. She knows her limitations, and she knows to differ right from wrong. I liked her and she never once betrayed my expectations....I like that she is being honest to herself and that she admits that she is in love with Reyn. Some scenes between the two were very funny, like:<br><br><blockquote>“You’re—you’re really not that good-looking,” I finally snapped. His eyes opened slightly—he had probably expected a comeback of somewhat higher quality. “Your nose is too pointy.” I was mortified to see my chest heave as I sucked in breath. “Your lips are too thin, you’re too tall, and your hair is really more brownish, not gold. Your eyes are small and squinty!”<br>Now he was looking at me as if he’d never seen someone having a psychotic break before and found it fascinating.<br>I flung down my dish towel, humiliated to be doing something so—clichéd. “Plus,” I hissed, “you’re such an asshole!” </blockquote><br><br>And she still thinks he is hot xD. Buuuuuuuuut..........there were some things that still shocked me.<br><br>Other than that, she has lived for 459 years, but being in bad company made her closed to others, shy, and not so revealing type. Once she witnessed what her own best friend was capable off, including breaking the taxi driver's spine for amusement, shocked her to the core. She run away soon after that, trying to understand why she followed her friends to party instead of helping poor man. She felt guilt and she wanted redemption, she understood that she needed change.<br><br>As for her life, previous one, i didn't quite expect anything, but i got something interesting....Especially the part with concerning someone.... <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Reyn</u>
  </i>
</b>: was all doom and gloom and i-do-not-want-you-here type. He was way to withdrawn, quiet and guarded. He also keeps his emotions under tight control. But the revelation about him and his past was something quite interesting. Where i was like:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399972ra/774568.gif" width="400" height="320" alt="nonononono" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>His relationship with Nasty though, was something quite else. It is not rushed, they didn't even interact so much between themselves. <br>Oh and how i laughed about the ways Nasty called him: Viking, Viking god, Odin, and things like that. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Others</u>
  </i>
</b>: I liked Dray, the gothic girl, and i liked River, the wise leader of all. On the other hand, that Incy guy has much issues... xD Or he is just obsessed with Nasty way to much. <br>As for Nell....i think the next img shows enough of what i think about her:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399972ra/774569.gif" width="250" height="140" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Overall</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br>Fun, fun, fun, fun, fun, fun, fun, fun, fun, fun, fun, fun, fun book :D<br>Well, not much of a LOL type, but it was highly entertaining read.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399972ra/774570.gif" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>My body is ready for second one &gt;:D<br><br>____________________________________________<br><br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br>____________________________________________ <br><br><b>REVIEW(S) RELATED TO THIS BOOK:</b><br><br>&gt;&gt; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/471576547" rel="nofollow noopener"> Immortal Beloved (Immortal Beloved, #1) </a> &lt;&lt;<br>&gt;&gt; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/471576567" rel="nofollow noopener"> Darkness Falls (Immortal Beloved, #2) </a> &lt;&lt;<br>&gt;&gt; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/471576580" rel="nofollow noopener"> Eternally Yours (Immortal Beloved, #3) </a> &lt;&lt;</span>

<div id="review_113065034" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113065034" />
    <a title="Misty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1124284-misty"><img alt="Misty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539720622p2/1124284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113065034?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misty" href="/user/show/1124284-misty">Misty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=juvenile-ya">juvenile-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=supernatural-paranormal">supernatural-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=sci_fi-fantasy">sci_fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=arc-or-galley">arc-or-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=ala-2010">ala-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113065034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5188692384335074013">Weirdly, unexpectedly, I was sort of amazed by this.  I'd heard of Cate Tiernan but never read anything by her.  I'd had friends  that pushed this on me (especially one who shall remain <a href='http://theallureofbooks.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'><s>Allison</s> </a>nameless).  It has a grandiose, somewhat silly title that I can't help but like because it reminds me of <a href='http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0110116/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gary Oldman and Beethoven</a>.   But somehow I still just wasn't expecting much from it.  Maybe it was the idea of an eternal club kid that just made me turn up my nose and say, Um, <i>no</i>.  But for all of the</span>
  <span id="freeText5188692384335074013" style="display:none">Weirdly, unexpectedly, I was sort of amazed by this.  I'd heard of Cate Tiernan but never read anything by her.  I'd had friends  that pushed this on me (especially one who shall remain <a href="http://theallureofbooks.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><s>Allison</s> </a>nameless).  It has a grandiose, somewhat silly title that I can't help but like because it reminds me of <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0110116/" rel="nofollow noopener">Gary Oldman and Beethoven</a>.   But somehow I still just wasn't expecting much from it.  Maybe it was the idea of an eternal club kid that just made me turn up my nose and say, Um, <i>no</i>.  But for all of the good I've heard about Cate Tiernan, I went into this with my expectations low.  And the b*itch proved me wrong.<br>I friggin loved it.<br><br>There were so many times it could have gone wrong - even <i>should</i> have gone wrong.  So many pet peeves and really bad tropes that had the potential to just kill it <i>dead</i>. And yet, Cate Tiernan not only made those pet-peevish things work, she made me like them. She made me say, yeah, ok. I'm with you. <br>460 year old club kid? Sure. <br>Protag who is powerful and special and gosh darn incredible without realizing it?  Okay.<br>Melodrama, crazy instant attraction, and a healthy dose of angst?  Bring it.<br>Viking alpha male almost-rapeyness?  <i>Why the eff not?</i> <br><br>I don't understand it.  If you had mentioned even one of those things, I probably would have quirked an eyebrow and said "Pass".  I would never have conceded to the possibility that I might end up liking any one of them.  <u>But I did</u>.  Like, a lot. <br>Cate Tiernan, you're a crafty one.  I understand why you write about witches, because clearly you are one.<br><br>I have to say, I <i>love</i> when someone proves me wrong. I love when someone takes something that I think is never going to work, and then <i>makes it work</i>.*  In less skillful hands, so much of this could have been very bad.  In less skillful hands, this book could have ended by being tossed against a wall, and this review could have been a rant.  But I <i>wasn't</i> irritated.  I didn't hate everything.  I didn't hate <i>anything</i>.  I feel vaguely warm and fuzzy. It's more than a little unsettling.<br><br>I could tell you all of the reasons that it worked, or all of the things I really liked, like how it was a great set-up for the series and had interesting world-building. Or how I really liked Nas and wanted to know more about her, <i>and</i> Reyn, <i>and </i>River <i>and </i>Incy, and all the rest.  I could tell you about how the flashbacks kept me intrigued and flowed well, rather than feeling abrupt and "foreshadowy" and pissing me off.  I could tell you about how it handles the concept of immortality better than just about any vampire/immortal/paranormal YA out there, or how it has this almost epic feel to it.<br><br>I could tell you all of those things, but what would be the point?  All I really want to tell you is to pick this one up and give it a chance, and let you find those things out for yourself.<br><br>Immortal Beloved was a strong start to a promising series - really <i>really <b>really </b></i>readable and engaging, and I definitely get the appeal of Cate Tiernan now.  I love when something thwarts my inner bitch and robs me of a good rant.<br>I like you Cate Tiernan; I've got my eye on you...<br><br><br><b>~ Other shiny editions ~</b><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8076197.Immortal_Beloved__Immortal_Beloved___1_" title="Immortal Beloved (Immortal Beloved, #1) by Cate Tiernan" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1327364099s/8076197.jpg" alt="Immortal Beloved (Immortal Beloved, #1) by Cate Tiernan" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9642425.Immortels__Immortels___1_" title="Immortels (Immortels, #1) by Cate Tiernan" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1288876053s/9642425.jpg" alt="Immortels (Immortels, #1) by Cate Tiernan" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9043380.Immortal_Beloved" title="Immortal Beloved by Cate Tiernan" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1282683717s/9043380.jpg" alt="Immortal Beloved by Cate Tiernan" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10043653.Immortal_Beloved_Entflammt" title="Immortal Beloved Entflammt by Cate Tiernan" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1327675971s/10043653.jpg" alt="Immortal Beloved Entflammt by Cate Tiernan" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>*Did anyone else just hearTim Gunn in their head?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337580i/695110.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_89006265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89006265" />
    <a title="Nafiza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2483439-nafiza"><img alt="Nafiza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529831446p2/2483439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89006265?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nafiza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nafiza" href="/user/show/2483439-nafiza">Nafiza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2483439-nafiza?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2483439-nafiza?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2483439-nafiza?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89006265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10516902768211247077">Let me start off by saying that I loved Cate Tiernan’s Sweep series. I must have read them more than a dozen times. Okay, I loved them all except for the last book where the main character gets old. Afraid of my mortality? Who me? No, of course not. But anyway, point is, I like Cate Tiernan’s writing. I like her characterizations and, most of all, I like her plotting. Suffice it to say that she’s mostly brilliant in my opinion. So when I found out that there was a new book coming out by her, I w</span>
  <span id="freeText10516902768211247077" style="display:none">Let me start off by saying that I loved Cate Tiernan’s Sweep series. I must have read them more than a dozen times. Okay, I loved them all except for the last book where the main character gets old. Afraid of my mortality? Who me? No, of course not. But anyway, point is, I like Cate Tiernan’s writing. I like her characterizations and, most of all, I like her plotting. Suffice it to say that she’s mostly brilliant in my opinion. So when I found out that there was a new book coming out by her, I was excited. Because, hello, awesome books will make for awesome reading. Okay, potentially awesome. I didn’t get to read it until some months after it was released but before that I read some reviews and they were mostly of the mixed variety. I was not really perturbed. Reading is so subjective. But I finally did read it and let me say this: It was awesome.<br /><br />I love, love, love flawed characters. I know they walk a thin line where they can easily become unlikeable but I felt Tiernan created Nastasya with just the right mix of spunk and irreverence. What she has been through, what she has experienced and seen does justify her attitudes. And she is irreverent, even caustic at times, very bratty but the reader senses early on that this attitude is a front she has nailed into place so that she is not vulnerable to the world and it’s many ways of hurting her. Is she annoying? I certainly didn’t think so. Her voice is fresh and compelling and her unwilling acceptance of her own imperfections are paired with just the right amount of disgruntlement that you can’t help but be won over.<br /><br />Tiernan has proved herself a master of weaving mythology through her narrative flawlessly. As she did with the Sweep series, she does so again with Immortal Beloved. The “immortals” are becoming a popular trope in both adult and YA paranormal novels and, like every other thing that is regurgitated endlessly, there is a potential for this theme to be overused. However, I like how Tiernan does not gloss over the negative side of what it means to live forever. She doesn’t romanticize the whole issue either. I won’t go so far as to say that it was wholly realistic, it is a YA paranormal novel after all, but I will say that it was tinged with a lot more realism than many books dealing with the same things. Nastasya has been married, she has been a mother, a widow – she has had multiple lifetimes and these things are bound to change a person’s perceptions of the world – I am not sure you can even call her a YA heroine. However, she does retain a sharp wit, an understanding of her own self and that vulnerability that is so reminiscent of the teenage years.<br /><br />On to the love interest. Reyn. There is no, “he is perfect, I want to knit him woolly scarves” kind of vibe here. There’s attraction, of course. Lots and lots of attraction. The kind that will have you fanning yourself or choking back a laugh at one of Nastasya’s wry remarks. But the attraction is tempered by many other issues which are remain important despite being historical. I like Reyn. Nastasya likes…well, I wouldn’t say she likes him but she does uh…like him. Yes. Anyway, he is an intriguing love interest.<br /><br />Other characters. Nastasya’s “friends” remain interesting though largely absent in the story. I am sort of glad about that because they seem like people beings I wouldn’t want to have contact with. Obviously Nastasya is going to need to confront them, perhaps in the next book but until then, they remain psychotic. Other characters at the “rehab” station that Nastasya ends up at are interesting. They are shadowy though and ambiguous but since the story is told in first person, I am not too concerned about it. Nastasya’s voice is loud enough.<br /><br />Anyway, I thoroughly enjoyed this book. I loved the idea of a rehab for immortal beings, being brought back to nature, trying to find value in time again when they have so much of it. I like Nastasya’s prickly composition and Reyn’s dense stoic self. The mythology is well constructed and the setting is detailed. I think you should give this book a chance if you haven’t done so already. If nothing else, you’ll enjoy a laugh or two or many. I know I can’t wait for the next one in the trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10516902768211247077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_131158941" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131158941" />
    <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden"><img alt="Katrina Passick Lumsden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416959676p2/1964146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131158941?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katrina Passick Lumsden" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden">Katrina Passick Lumsden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden?shelf=pleasantly-surprised">pleasantly-surprised</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131158941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15852896205295372287">I absolutely love this book. It surprised me because I've read some of Cate Tiernan's Sweep series and, while I enjoyed those, they never in a million years would have led me to believe Teirnan was capable of the kind of writing I encountered in Immortal Beloved. <br/><br/>The characters are believable, beautifully flawed, and interesting. The dialog is simple and realistic. The romance alternates between sweet, confusing, terrifying, and heart-wrenching. At first glance it may appear that the protagonist</span>
  <span id="freeText15852896205295372287" style="display:none">I absolutely love this book. It surprised me because I've read some of Cate Tiernan's Sweep series and, while I enjoyed those, they never in a million years would have led me to believe Teirnan was capable of the kind of writing I encountered in Immortal Beloved. <br /><br />The characters are believable, beautifully flawed, and interesting. The dialog is simple and realistic. The romance alternates between sweet, confusing, terrifying, and heart-wrenching. At first glance it may appear that the protagonist is awfully immature for someone who's been around for over 400 years, but that's kind of the point Tiernan's making; Nastasya IS immature. And she's immature because she's spent 459 years avoiding her traumatizing past and refusing to grow up. <br /><br />This book combines a little romance with the supernatural world of Immortals, but it's mostly about Nastasya's struggle to find herself, and that journey isn't an easy one for her. I loved her as a character. She's strong and funny, but there is an underlying fragility that keeps her from coming off as uber-bitchy. <br /><br />The love interest, Reyn, is not your typical supernatural YA hunk, either. He's a villain who's reformed, sure, but he's not wallowing around in self pity or trying to come off as a bad ass. While he seems genuinely contrite regarding his past behaviors, he knows he can neither justify them nor will them away. No projections or illusions with Reyn and that makes for a thoroughly enjoyable character.<br /><br />There's a small bit of mystery interlaced as we travel with Nastasya through her memories and slowly uncover who she is and where she came from (and the mysterious tie that she and Reyn share). There's also rivalry in the form of a younger immortal who is vying for Reyn's attention. Not to mention some rather unsavory friends of Nastasya's who are out looking for her when she doesn't want to be found. <br /><br />I found this book altogether enjoyable and completely worthy of a second, third, and maybe fourth read. The only complaint I have is that I have to wait until September for the next in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15852896205295372287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="WillowBe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="WillowBe" href="/user/show/1842059-willowbe">WillowBe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9336671115921134189">I LOVE this story. I LOVE it so much, I stopped reading it. I will control myself and wait for the other two books in the trilogy to come out so that I won't sit around bemoaning the wait. I am so into this story, so into the guy, that I just need to back off. This is the type of teen book that easily satifies an adult reader. These charactars are less immortal teenagers than immortal beings that happen to look like teens, but don't necessarily act like them. The charactar's navigation of the ti</span>
  <span id="freeText9336671115921134189" style="display:none">I LOVE this story. I LOVE it so much, I stopped reading it. I will control myself and wait for the other two books in the trilogy to come out so that I won't sit around bemoaning the wait. I am so into this story, so into the guy, that I just need to back off. This is the type of teen book that easily satifies an adult reader. These charactars are less immortal teenagers than immortal beings that happen to look like teens, but don't necessarily act like them. The charactar's navigation of the timeless issues of loss, redemption and the difficulty of making moral choices daily is riveting. The existential angst is what I find intriguing; it adds depth to the tension, caused by the suspense of the overt mystery that carries the books events (which any adult reader of paranormal fic will easily unravel). And no vampires were used in the making of this book!<br /><br />BTW IB reminds me a bit of Sarah Rees Brennan trilogy- the Demon's Lexicon, Covenant- two other books by an Irish writer that I wish I'd waited for the trilogy to be completed before I started reading. Ms. Tiernan is a much better writer, or rather her experience and mastery of the form is evident in her prose.</span>

<div id="review_218818367" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218818367" />
    <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218818367?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316035910" href="/book/show/8961636-immortal-beloved">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=heroines-i-adore">heroines-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=i-just-have-a-lot-of-feelings">i-just-have-a-lot-of-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=hilarious">hilarious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=oh-my-god-marry-me">oh-my-god-marry-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218818367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10620093061404852784">This review is also available over at <a href='http://wildheartbookblogs.blogspot.com/2012/06/review-immortal-beloved-by-cate-tiernan.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>my blog.</a><br/><br/>__________________________<br/><br/>This book is probably my most favorite book about immortals that I've read so far.<br/><br/>Nastasya─or Nasty, as her friends call her─is a 459-year-old immortal who's been living life and partying with her crew of other immortals. Until one night, her best friend Innocencio─Incy, for short─tortures a cabbie right in front of her, and she's suddenly filled with fear and decides to run away, seeking a house called the River's Edge. She</span>
  <span id="freeText10620093061404852784" style="display:none">This review is also available over at <a href="http://wildheartbookblogs.blogspot.com/2012/06/review-immortal-beloved-by-cate-tiernan.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog.</a><br /><br />__________________________<br /><br />This book is probably my most favorite book about immortals that I've read so far.<br /><br />Nastasya─or Nasty, as her friends call her─is a 459-year-old immortal who's been living life and partying with her crew of other immortals. Until one night, her best friend Innocencio─Incy, for short─tortures a cabbie right in front of her, and she's suddenly filled with fear and decides to run away, seeking a house called the River's Edge. She soon finds out that the house is a rehab for wayward immortals, and there she meets River, the owner of the house, and Reyn, the fellow immortal that she can't help but be attracted to, but who she finds is somewhat familiar to her. Just when Nasty thought she was going to belong there, she finds out that someone wants her dead.<br /><br />I definitely noticed the difference from other YA immortal books out there. Most immortal books in YA tell of a regular human girl meeting the mysterious immortal boy, but this one is so much more than that. Nastasya is an immortal girl who has really been through everything. What I loved about this book are the flashbacks and memories of Nastasya's life in different times, and also when she was still very young, before she knew of her immortality. Most of those scenes were very heart-wrenching for me, mostly due to how graphic they are.<br /><br />Nasty is just awesome. I loved her attitude and her way of thinking, and how she would call Reyn, the love interest, the Viking god or Odin the Odious. She definitely made me giggle and smile a lot, and she was just overall a very likable protagonist.<br /><br />Reyn . . . He's actually a love interest that was hard for me to figure out. He wasn't a jerk, no. He was . . . I don't know. Quiet, dense, I never really connected to him. But I loved the big reveal about him, and Nasty's overall relationship with him. There was nothing rushed at all about their romance. We barely even get to see it, besides some sexual tension here and there, but there will probably be a lot of it in the next book.<br /><br />Nell was the bitchy character in the book, but she had a nice facade in the beginning. But the more and more you progress through the book, the more you would notice her start to crumble and lose her cool. But even though I hate her guts, I'll admit she did make the book a lot more interesting.<br /><br />River is the owner of the River's Edge house, and she's about 1300 years old. I did like her, but there wasn't much about her that stuck out to me. I liked the other minor characters in the house too.<br /><br />What I also loved is how the immortal thing works in this book, and what the purpose of the River's Edge house is. Every immortal is born Terava─meaning evil or dark. At River's Edge, the immortals are taught to appreciate the little things in life, and to become Tahti─meaning good. But once you do become good, that doesn't mean it'll stick. You will have to make sure to stay good, and not give in to dark magick, thus becoming Terava again. I thought that was very interesting.<br /><br />I definitely get why I've seen a lot of positive reviews for this book, and I'm very excited to see where this series will go. I already recently bought the second book and can't wait to read it! I would recommend this book to you if you want a great YA book about immortals, because most of the other ones I've read had never impressed me as this book had.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10620093061404852784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_110553231" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110553231" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/202724-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601676054p2/202724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110553231?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/202724-jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=all-timefavorites">all-timefavorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110553231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4420775230033305699">I picked this up as an ARC at ALA, mostly because I saw the words "Viking god" on the back, then promptly stuck it on the bottom of my "to read" pile. MISTAKE! I should have read it immediately! What a fabulous book! I was giddy as I read it. GIDDY!<br/><br/>First of all in our things to love: our protag, Nastasya, a name that I didn't care for, and thought on the first page, "I'm going to hate her soon, because of her name." But it isn't her real name, it's not even close, and the reason why no one has c</span>
  <span id="freeText4420775230033305699" style="display:none">I picked this up as an ARC at ALA, mostly because I saw the words "Viking god" on the back, then promptly stuck it on the bottom of my "to read" pile. MISTAKE! I should have read it immediately! What a fabulous book! I was giddy as I read it. GIDDY!<br /><br />First of all in our things to love: our protag, Nastasya, a name that I didn't care for, and thought on the first page, "I'm going to hate her soon, because of her name." But it isn't her real name, it's not even close, and the reason why no one has called her her real name in centuries is revealed in heart-breaking little flashes. She's a heroine that you soon grow to love, because she feels herself to be unlovable, but not in a self-suffering, oh-poor-me way. She's very matter-of-fact about it. She's done terrible things, suffered some very real horrors, and hates herself as much as she thinks anyone hates her. She has a tender place in her heart, however, for teenage girls like the one she used to be. She has a sharp sense of humor, and wields sarcasm as delicately as a rapier. (Anyone who says sarcasm is the lowest form of humor has clearly not heard it done right.) I was howling with laughter at the things she said, and thought, and her discovery that she can get rid of her boss by asking him to do a price check on Kotex is the best. thing. ever.<br /><br />More to love? The very realistic look at immortality. After four hundred years, Nastasya has literally seen and done it all. She's traveled the world, eaten every kind of food, done every sort of vice, been married, had kids, tried everything a human can try. Now what? The average immortal is, essentially, a partier. Because they can drink all night, sleep with anyone who crosses their path, and then walk away from it all. No cirrhosis of the liver. No lung cancer. No STD can stop them. And the weight of the years, and decades, starts to wear on them until they will do anything to numb the pain for a day or an hour. They have magic, but for most of them it means drawing on the lfie force of others, leaving animals and plants dead in their wake, and for what? A party trick that impresses your friends and makes you forget your dead loved ones for a few minutes? So what do you do, and how do you make it all stop?<br /><br />Intrigued yet? YOU SHOULD BE! Go, grab a copy of this book, and hold it to your bosom for a just a moment before you dive into one of the best books you'll read this year!<br /><br />And remember: when you're buying pants, most people try them on first.<br /><br />11/15/12 Reread: Loved just as much as the first time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4420775230033305699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14141950030802015460" style="display:none"><b>DETAILS</b><br><i>IMMORTAL BELOVED #1<br>BY CATE TIERNAN<br>NARRATION: KELLY LINTZ<br>URBAN FANTASY<br>PARANORMAL ROMANCE<br>MAGIC</i><br><br><b>BOOK THEME SONG:</b><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cu7QvOQKcKk" rel="nofollow noopener">My Immortal</a><br><br><b>MY RATING: 4/5 STARS<br><br>MY THOUGHTS<br><br>FIRST IMPRESSION</b>: Immortals who are not Vampires…I think I like this. <br><br><b>MY REVIEW IN ONE SENTENCE</b>: A slow-burning, contemplative tale...that is both historical and contemporary.<br><br>Nastasya has lived an incredibly long life and because of this, she has so many stories to tell. This story actually snuck up on me slowly, there isn't a lot of action, but there is a lot of introspection. I do have to say for someone who has lived as long as she has…she has a lot of growing up to do. With that being said, I still think she is a cool, and seriously badass chic. I liked her because she seems to be on the right path now.<br><br>The world of Immortal Beloved is alluring yet intimidating. It seems to me living that long could get really boring, especially with the life she had been living. On the other hand, think of all the books you could read with that kind of time.<br><br><br><b>BREAKDOWN</b><br><i>Plot: 4/5<br>Characters: 5/5<br>The Feels: 4.2/5<br>Theme: 4/5<br>Flow: 5/5 <br>Backdrop (World Building): 5/5 <br>Originality: 4/5 <br>Book Cover: 4/5 <br>Narration: 4/5 <br>Ending: 3.5/5.
